  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e8067e09-a262-4cfe-a4a9-c79028276f04'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer18213538711781425834">The astonishing debut novel from international number one bestselling author Paullina Simons, now beautifully repackaged <br/><br/>Tully Makker is a tough young woman from the wrong side of the tracks and she is not always easy to like.   <span id="freeText18213538711781425834" style="display:none">The astonishing debut novel from international number one bestselling author Paullina Simons, now beautifully repackaged <br /><br />Tully Makker is a tough young woman from the wrong side of the tracks and she is not always easy to like. But if Tully gives friendship and loyalty, she gives them for good, and she forms an enduring bond with Jennifer and Julie, school friends from very different backgrounds. As they grow into the world of the seventies and eighties, the lives of the three best friends are changed forever by two young men, Robin and Jack, and a tragedy which engulfs them all. Against the odds, Tully emerges into young womanhood, marriage and a career. At last Tully Makker has life under control. And then life strikes back in the most unexpected way of all...</span>

<div id="review_71692619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71692619" />
    <a title="Ivy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2307899-ivy"><img alt="Ivy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287970433p2/2307899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71692619?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivy" href="/user/show/2307899-ivy">Ivy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312954215" href="/book/show/1372968.Tully">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71692619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15722059023839490639">I never thought I would hate a novel by Paullina Simons, but here it is. This overly long first novel deals with the life a young woman named Tully Makker. She comes from a horribly abusive family and her background, as well as tragic loss, sets the stage for the poor life choices she makes throughout the novel.<br/><br/>The plot moves at a turtle's pace taking us through Tully's devastating teen years where her mother's attentions range from nonexistant to severe beatings. Tully dances at frat parties an</span>
  <span id="freeText15722059023839490639" style="display:none">I never thought I would hate a novel by Paullina Simons, but here it is. This overly long first novel deals with the life a young woman named Tully Makker. She comes from a horribly abusive family and her background, as well as tragic loss, sets the stage for the poor life choices she makes throughout the novel.<br /><br />The plot moves at a turtle's pace taking us through Tully's devastating teen years where her mother's attentions range from nonexistant to severe beatings. Tully dances at frat parties and strip joints for money, loses herself in meaningless sex, and isolates herself from her best friends, Jennifer and Julie. When tragedy strikes, the loss is so overwhelming for Tully that it haunts her well into womanhood and influences her decisions. Tully continues to isolate herself, bouncing from man to man and, at times, two-timing her boyfriends. While all this is happening she is trying to decide the course of her future, but fails miserably because she refuses to share herself with people that might help her. She finally decides to go to college and study social work.<br /><br />The tone of this book was tragic and disappointing, overly long, and hopeless. (No I don't need to read a page and a half of how she convinces the state of Kansas to allow Child Services a bigger budget and longer training times for prospective foster families.) Tully then marries, out of neccesity, a man who loves her but she feels nothing for. People hate her at her job because she makes waves, her friend Shakie loves a fellow classmate but can't have him because she is married...blah, blah, blah. I was also dissatisfied with the way the relationship between Tully and her mother is wrapped up. It didn't feel realistic to me at all. I never felt any sympathy for her lovers except Jack. He didn't deserve to be hurt by Tully who seems to poison everything she touches.<br /><br />Towards the end of the book I hoped that Tully would finally get a little happiness and what does the idiot do? She makes another dumb choice. I felt my anger rising and I finally lost my patience with this drivel. Tully muddles through life and just when things seem to be changing for the better, she once again throws happiness away with both hands. I never thought I would dislike a heroine as much as I disliked this one. The entire book had me wondering what the point of it was? <br /><br />D+ read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15722059023839490639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I also remember it making me cry and my heart aching. <br/><br/>I'm not sure whether I would appreciate it in the same way today, now I'm older and wiser, but <i>Tully</i> is definitely a title that has stayed with me over the years, and each time I see the front cover it fills me w</span>
  <span id="freeText4368260210772739006" style="display:none">I read this book many years ago, in my late teens and loved it. <br /><br />Although I no longer remember the details, I do remember the book being long, and it taking over my life for quite a few days, as I was so taken in by the story it told. I also remember it making me cry and my heart aching. <br /><br />I'm not sure whether I would appreciate it in the same way today, now I'm older and wiser, but <i>Tully</i> is definitely a title that has stayed with me over the years, and each time I see the front cover it fills me with feelings of anguish and sadness, as if I'm back within the pages of the book again.<br /><br />If you like the sound of the blurb, I recommend this one. I imagine if I read it today it would probably make me feel nostalgic about my days growing up. It might also appeal to fans of Young Adult fiction or teenage readers too.</span>

  <span id="freeText4941232270639180585" style="display:none">I’m not really sure how to rate this book. Reading it involved a lot of eye rolling and cursing out loud every other page. I think my loathing was more for the characters than for any faulty writing or for the book itself. I have never read about a character that I loathed more than Tully, which I suppose is better than being completely indifferent. I finished it. It was a 400+ page novel and I finished it simply because I admit – begrudgingly – that the story, as horrible as it was, was engaging. It was kind of like those awful made-for-TV movies that you complain about and yet, two hours later, there you are, still watching it. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_108923364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108923364" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3591452-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302976286p2/3591452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108923364?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/3591452-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108923364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7573102371629517826">Tully Makker is a survivor. She survives her father's abandonment at the age of 7. She survives her uncle's "attentions" at the age of 12. She survives her mother's abusive hands throughout her childhood and adolescence. Her best friend's betrayal in her senior year of high school is the hardest for Tully to survive. She survives....but not without scars....scars on her wrists, scars that haunt her in her sleep, scars upon her heart. There are those who try to help Tully throughout her life. The</span>
  <span id="freeText7573102371629517826" style="display:none">Tully Makker is a survivor. She survives her father's abandonment at the age of 7. She survives her uncle's "attentions" at the age of 12. She survives her mother's abusive hands throughout her childhood and adolescence. Her best friend's betrayal in her senior year of high school is the hardest for Tully to survive. She survives....but not without scars....scars on her wrists, scars that haunt her in her sleep, scars upon her heart. There are those who try to help Tully throughout her life. There's Robin, a good man who loves her unconditionally with all of her scars. A man who asks nothing of her, who endures her silence and betrayal, and still loves her with every ounce of his being. There's Julie, one of her best friends from childhood. Yet she too is trying to come to terms with her own life and her own mistakes and regrets. And there's Jack, the man who open's Tully's eyes and her heart, who makes her face her grief, a grief he too shares.<br /><br />Undeniably, "Tully" is a story of survival and self-discovery. It's about a friendship so strong that it endures even beyond death. It is about a love so strong that it endures through months of absence and years of dreaming. What makes the character Tully so real is that she is far from perfect. She makes mistakes, big ones, mistakes that made me say "What the hell are you doing?" I disagreed with many of her choices, so much so that I wanted to shake some sense into her. But always throughout the story, I wanted Tully to take that step, to take off the armour, trust someone, let them in, let them help her unburden herself from all of the grief she carried around. I wanted her to see that her life was good....if she would only live it for herself.<br /><br /><br />Paullina Simons has fast become one of my favourite authors. She makes me adore her characters....fall in love with them...cheer for them...cry for them....mourn for them. She makes me find it within my heart to forgive them their sins...even when I wouldn't forgive myself the same sin. I cried a lot in this book, for the author has left the door open for me to examine my own life decisions, to ask the "what if" questions, to examine the skeletons in my closet. Sure, I have many regrets, and yes, my life could have been different. But like Tully.....I have survived.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7573102371629517826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_195924206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195924206" />
    <a title="Ashleigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5986965-ashleigh"><img alt="Ashleigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405452282p2/5986965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195924206?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh" href="/user/show/5986965-ashleigh">Ashleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195924206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18222657274246054507">I struggled to give "Tully" three stars. This book started out really intriguing - the first third of the book I thouroughly enjoyed. As I started to get into the middle of the book, I realised that it would have greatly benefited from proper editing. It is obvious that 'Tully' is Paulina Simon's first book, and at times it seems she has something to prove. <br/><br/>This book was far, far too long. It repeated itself so much and drew out unecessary sub-plots with too much description. Halfway through the</span>
  <span id="freeText18222657274246054507" style="display:none">I struggled to give "Tully" three stars. This book started out really intriguing - the first third of the book I thouroughly enjoyed. As I started to get into the middle of the book, I realised that it would have greatly benefited from proper editing. It is obvious that 'Tully' is Paulina Simon's first book, and at times it seems she has something to prove. <br /><br />This book was far, far too long. It repeated itself so much and drew out unecessary sub-plots with too much description. Halfway through the book, I was wondering where it was going and why I was still reading it. The main character, Tully is absoloutley awful and extrememly hard to like or empathise with. Also, the way the men in her life stick with her despite all the things she does and how poorly she treats everyone is very unbelievable. Throughout the whole book, I just kept feeling like every emotion was fake - Tully's 20 year grief for her friend, her undying hatred of her Mother, her relationships with Robin, Jack and Jeremy. There were also so many characters whose storyline's were just written out with no explanation. I felt as though Jeremy, Julie, Tully's Father, Shakie and many others were an unecessary addition to the story. I also had trouble understanding why anyone wanted anything to do with Tully at all, I found myself getting very frustrated with this book. <br /><br />Also, the character's names were a turn-off. For some reason, I just couldn't believe there were characters called Shakie and Boomerang, among others. <br /><br />The biggest dissapointment of this book - which originally showed so much promise - was the arduous, drawn out ending, which was a total anti-climax. I kept expecting the story to go somewhere - instead it went around in circles. I felt cheated that I came to the end of such a long and painful read only to find the ending was so dissapointing, and the author could have cut out half the book and the ending still would have been the same and made sense.<br /><br />Overall, I was dissapointed in 'Tully' and frustrated throughout the course of reading the story. It was a good attempt at a first novel but would have greatly benefited from a serious edit and reshaping of the story. At first I liked this book, but with each page, I grew to dislike it more and more. It was a struggle to finish, and not worth the time it takes to read it. Unfortunate, as it did show some promise. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18222657274246054507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127483006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127483006" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2120940-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289055741p2/2120940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127483006?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/2120940-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127483006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6731377011836343789">One of the most intense books I have ever read. <br/> <br/>Tully is about a group of high school friends that are each individually shattered by a specific tragedy that befalls one of them. And this book shows how this tragedy shapes their lives, pushes them apart, and eventually brings them back together. It follows a small group over the course of a decade and shows how people either learn to cope with grief and loss or they let it destroy them. Tully is the main character and she was horridly abused an</span>
  <span id="freeText6731377011836343789" style="display:none">One of the most intense books I have ever read. <br /> <br />Tully is about a group of high school friends that are each individually shattered by a specific tragedy that befalls one of them. And this book shows how this tragedy shapes their lives, pushes them apart, and eventually brings them back together. It follows a small group over the course of a decade and shows how people either learn to cope with grief and loss or they let it destroy them. Tully is the main character and she was horridly abused and neglected during her childhood. She was already on a path of self-destruction when the tragedy throws her even more off the course of normalcy. This girl is out of control. Yet, in the midst of suffering--and the depressive nature of most of this book--there is a subtle, but very present message about the healing power of unconditional love; it binds this girl to two men who are at the heart of the tragedy from her youth. I don't want to say too much more about the plot. <br /> <br />Like all of Paullina Simons's books, Tully is not sugar-coated. The hard times these characters face are totally fleshed-out. Attention to detail is impeccible. Sometimes I hated the main character because of the choices she made, but I was always rooting for her--because deep down I knew Tully was a product of her past just trying to survive. This book was hard for me to get through at times, but I could not put it down. Ever. I think my heart broke 10 different times.<br /><br />It is not my typical kind of book, but it got me thinking. There were definite times when the characters made horrible, selfish decisions. By the end, I felt like I needed some alcohol to relax....and I kept asking myself "Did I even like this book considering the final course of the story?" <br /> <br />Yes, I really did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6731377011836343789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135761166" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135761166" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1873554-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576464969p2/1873554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135761166?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/1873554-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer135761166&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135761166" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6150347335456400070">I finished the book at 3 o'clock in the morning and I'm still not sure how to feel about it. It's not one that I want to read again and if I had read this one before "The Bronze Horseman" I'm not sure I would've picked up another one of her books.<br/><br/>Throughout the whole thing, I really wasn't sure how I felt about Tully and the relationships she had with people. Her relationship with Jack was all based, I felt, on the fact that he had once been with Jennifer; she just transferred her feelings for J</span>
  <span id="freeText6150347335456400070" style="display:none">I finished the book at 3 o'clock in the morning and I'm still not sure how to feel about it. It's not one that I want to read again and if I had read this one before "The Bronze Horseman" I'm not sure I would've picked up another one of her books.<br /><br />Throughout the whole thing, I really wasn't sure how I felt about Tully and the relationships she had with people. Her relationship with Jack was all based, I felt, on the fact that he had once been with Jennifer; she just transferred her feelings for Jennifer to Jack, to a more acceptable form of love. Jack was in love with her in high school, I'm sure and so when she finally started loving him, he didn't turn her away.<br /><br />Her relationship with Robin is one I'll never get - I honestly don't understand how someone can just turn a blind eye to something like that. Perhaps it's because I've never been in love with someone so much that I wouuld do anything to keep them that I look at Robin and I think "you poor sap - what the hell were you thinking?"<br /><br />Hedda - don't even get me started on that one. I think that's why Tully went to work for the foster system. She saw it as a way to save other children from the same torture and abuse that she went through. What I don't understand is how Hedda didn't understand that what wahat she did to Tully in her childhold directly affected the way Tully treated her when she was an adult. I also really couldn't stand the way that Robin just basically looked at Tully and said "Get over it and treat your mother with some respect." That was the real issue I think with their relationship is that Robin couldn't seperate his feelings for his dead mother with the feelings that Tully had for her mother, who though she was still allive, was in all senses dead to her the meant Tully pointed that gun at Hedda in the first section.<br /><br />All in all, this book really kind of sent me on a downer - Tully's life was so depressing and she had so many opportunities to change that she didn't take that I almost feel no sorrow for her or pity. It's a lesson in take your life into your own hands and don't worry about what eother people think when you know that nothing where you are is good for you anymore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6150347335456400070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7440938898288015887">I'm more than overwhelmed, I'm partially broken.<br/><br/>I think it would be helpful to get a mental image of what my poor husband had to deal with while I was reading this book...me crying my eyes out on the couch...me waking him up in the middle of the night making sure he was happy in our marriage. (By which I mean, I woke him up...then asked him if he was happy..."I was happy when I was asleep...yes...can I go back to sleep now")?<br/>It's lucky that my poor hubby is very aware of how baseline crazy I am </span>
  <span id="freeText7440938898288015887" style="display:none">I'm more than overwhelmed, I'm partially broken.<br /><br />I think it would be helpful to get a mental image of what my poor husband had to deal with while I was reading this book...me crying my eyes out on the couch...me waking him up in the middle of the night making sure he was happy in our marriage. (By which I mean, I woke him up...then asked him if he was happy..."I was happy when I was asleep...yes...can I go back to sleep now")?<br />It's lucky that my poor hubby is very aware of how baseline crazy I am that he doesn't suspect I'm having an affair with how many times I've asked him if he would "forgive me if I ever..."<br /><br />Suffice it to say this book straight up mind-fucked me.<br />Now to the review...<br /><br />I know that a lot of people didn't like the character of Tully... I LOVED her. I completely and totally related to her. The only person she ever was capable of loving for the majority of her life...was Jennifer. Her best friend. I am blessed with a best friend that is that exact person to me. If I lost her...I would break. So I get her...I get her completely. <br />Let's not even get into her childhood...I am in awe of her strength and her ability to channel that into her future career. Which she totally dominated in.<br />In my job, I see things people don't get to un-see, I know the need to emotionally unload before you get home and the difficulty to relate to other "normals" who have no idea the horrible underbelly reality.<br /><br />Robin and Jack: trying really hard to say something without spoilers...<br />I LOVED Robin... I don't think I could have cried harder for this man. Let me say it again... I LOVED Robin. <br />I also really loved Jack. I was smitten. I'm not going to lie, I would have likely done the EXACT same thing as in the book. <br /><br />I would do ANYTHING for an epilogue...something...just to make my brain relax a little.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2229301728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2229301728" />
    <a title="Zoe (Attic Salt Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43972006-zoe-attic-salt-reviews"><img alt="Zoe (Attic Salt Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508845795p2/43972006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2229301728?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe (Attic Salt Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe (Attic Salt Reviews)" href="/user/show/43972006-zoe-attic-salt-reviews">Zoe (Attic Salt Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2229301728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2175517289714400918">I am sorry to say that I really didn’t enjoy this book – every page making me want to give up entirely on the story. I don’t think I’ve ever rolled my eyes or scoffed in disgust so much in any book before.<br/><br/>The story follows Tully Makker, a wild young woman, as she navigates a life filled with tragedy and hardship. The painfully drawn out plot takes readers through Tully’s teen years, where she throws herself into a life of parties, sex and alcohol in the hopes of avoiding her abusive mother all t</span>
  <span id="freeText2175517289714400918" style="display:none">I am sorry to say that I really didn’t enjoy this book – every page making me want to give up entirely on the story. I don’t think I’ve ever rolled my eyes or scoffed in disgust so much in any book before.<br><br>The story follows Tully Makker, a wild young woman, as she navigates a life filled with tragedy and hardship. The painfully drawn out plot takes readers through Tully’s teen years, where she throws herself into a life of parties, sex and alcohol in the hopes of avoiding her abusive mother all the while isolating herself from her two best friends, Jennifer and Julie. But a loss, one which Tully carries long into her adulthood, determines the tone of her future. Stupid decision after stupid decision, man after man and drink after drink, Tully’s life returns to the cycle of isolation, cheating and meaninglessness which had dominated the teen years she worked so hard to put behind her. <br><br>This book moved through Tully’s life slowly, never focusing on interesting or important events but spending a full two pages describing how she danced on a random guy that she never knew. Any time I found myself approaching what could have been a pivotal moment in the story, it was completely swept under a rug by the sorry combination of poor writing and a lack of emphasis on the moment. The story just moved on like nothing at all happened and so any emotion I felt was just washed away. It was the most disappointing thing to deal with.<br><br>And our main character didn’t help all that much either. I have no problem with saying I absolutely hated her. Tully was rude and cold to anyone who tried to show care or affection to her and refused to let anyone in, to let anyone know her. She constantly complained about people not loving her for her but, who is she? Not even I know! Tully spent the entirety of the novel leading on two men, who had fallen deeply in love with her, and complaining about it. She would say no to one but wind up in his bed by the end of the night.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518320097ra/25039160.gif" width="398" height="180" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for the supporting characters, they were equally shallow with equally disinteresting character arcs and I struggled to find anything vaguely admirable about the lot of them. No one liked their lives, everyone settled unhappily and broke their promises, none were loyal to their partners and it was really fucking annoying. <br><br>An entire story that tries to make me sympathise with a woman who got into her situation from making stupid decisions and being inconstant and then blaming everyone else for her regrets. I wouldn’t recommend Tully to anyone but I found myself constantly surprised by the number of people who actually loved reading it – I can’t say I understand why but, who knows, you might like it…<br><br>Find my entire review on my blog <a href="http://atticsaltreviews.blogspot.com.au/2018/02/tully-paullina-simons.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2175517289714400918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18647598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18647598" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/918327-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326385184p2/918327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18647598?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/918327-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780002245906" href="/book/show/626233.Tully_">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All my girl friends</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amanda by: </span>
      Randomly found
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18647598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1135884782339479764">I started out this book with apprehension... oh great another coming of age story about a mistreated teenager...<br/><br/>However, I really liked the character Tully, and the story was original and entertaining. The author paints a very vivid picture (warning some very "naughty" scenes) and you very easily are taken back to the 80's. I would not consider this book a real "page turner," as I had no problem putting it down, but it was compelling enough to keep picking it up and wanting to know what was goin</span>
  <span id="freeText1135884782339479764" style="display:none">I started out this book with apprehension... oh great another coming of age story about a mistreated teenager...<br /><br />However, I really liked the character Tully, and the story was original and entertaining. The author paints a very vivid picture (warning some very "naughty" scenes) and you very easily are taken back to the 80's. I would not consider this book a real "page turner," as I had no problem putting it down, but it was compelling enough to keep picking it up and wanting to know what was going to happen to Tully. The themes in this novel were presented very clearly and formed slowly and approately so that there was a cathartic sense of understanding during the last chapters. This is one of those books that when finished reading I think, "yep, that's how life is." Even though I wouldn't necessarily have thought of it that way before reading the book. I found the novel to be very Anne Tyler in that way. <br /><br />This made me think about my own dreams and the things that should be let go of as I approach 30 myself and you start to realize that even though your life is not what you though it would be when you were a teenager or in your earlier twenty's it can still be ok. I think that I agree with Tully in that the best dream of all is to be dream free -- even if this doesn't necessarily mean having all your dreams come true. It sounds like I'm advocating giving up but it's really about reevaluating the value of what you already have. <br /><br />I actually purchased this first addition copy for resale, but I think I'll be keeping it for my own collection! This book will leave you with something to think about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1135884782339479764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1009057073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009057073" />
    <a title="Alexandria Hanson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33443648-alexandria-hanson"><img alt="Alexandria Hanson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406549447p2/33443648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009057073?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandria Hanson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandria Hanson" href="/user/show/33443648-alexandria-hanson">Alexandria Hanson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009057073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer787416877837274237">I very much enjoyed this book because it wasn't written to please readers in the hopes of them getting the character to do what they wanted them to do. People tend to love fairytales and the idea that life goes smoothly, but this book I felt portrayed the realities of many life circumstances and decisions. It centered around a very broken and selfish woman who made poor choices and good ones. I both loved and loathed Tully Makker at the same time. The fact that she was so selfish and played arou</span>
  <span id="freeText787416877837274237" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed this book because it wasn't written to please readers in the hopes of them getting the character to do what they wanted them to do. People tend to love fairytales and the idea that life goes smoothly, but this book I felt portrayed the realities of many life circumstances and decisions. It centered around a very broken and selfish woman who made poor choices and good ones. I both loved and loathed Tully Makker at the same time. The fact that she was so selfish and played around with good men had me gritting my teeth, but remembering that she was a victim of sexual abuse and rape as a child, her actions surrounding dancing in strip clubs, engaging in sexual activities with much older men and messing around with their lives seems understandable. To me in the back of her mind, it seemed she was punishing these men in order to get some satisfaction to herself. It seemed clear to me she punished her husband Robin with her cruelty, failure in duties as a wife to him and nonchalant way she had an affair for getting her pregnant. We all know she chose Jeremy first and wanted to leave her life in Kansas behind. As much as she loved her son I think the fact that she had to depend on Robin because of it built up some form of resentment within her. I suppose what I liked most about the book were the themes. Child abuse, negligence, the failure of social service systems, suicide and the resilience to come out as a strong successful person despite it all. Tully was an interesting character to read about. One of many complexities, hypocrisy and strife. In the end though I very much enjoyed the book and could barely put it down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="787416877837274237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103082648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103082648" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3300356-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271025577p2/3300356.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103082648?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/3300356-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103082648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13308594136966597970">PS introduces us to Tully, someone who has you experiencing lots of mixed emotions. She is a dark character with many secrets and a past that she wants to move on from, but a loveless childhood filled with anguish, abandonment and abuse is difficult to deal with. Tully makes certain choices through her life which leaves you feeling frustrated, sympathetic and emotional throughout the book.<br/><br/>She meets Jennifer and Julie who become her closest friends and help to fill the void and provide an escape </span>
  <span id="freeText13308594136966597970" style="display:none">PS introduces us to Tully, someone who has you experiencing lots of mixed emotions. She is a dark character with many secrets and a past that she wants to move on from, but a loveless childhood filled with anguish, abandonment and abuse is difficult to deal with. Tully makes certain choices through her life which leaves you feeling frustrated, sympathetic and emotional throughout the book.<br /><br />She meets Jennifer and Julie who become her closest friends and help to fill the void and provide an escape from an unhappy childhood. The many torturous dreams she experiences leaves Tully wanting to move on to a happy future. Along comes Robin who loves her unconditionally and wants nothing but for Tully to return his affections, and Jack who shares a connection with Tully through Jennifer. Tully is tormented with the past and struggles to leave it behind. A tragedy that strikes Tully to the core is something that changes her life and the path that she follows forever. The decisions and choices that she needs to make leave her tormented and emotionally drained.<br /><br />PS has provided yet another book that I thought was enthralling and captivating. Her capability to make you feel that you are there within the storyline, and asking yourself "what would I have done" in certain situations is something that I really enjoyed. <br /><br />I truly loved this book and PS is certainly one of my favourite authors!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13308594136966597970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer80982070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5723870225379258873">Tully Makker is a tough young woman from the wrong side of the tracks and she is not always easy to like. But if Tully gives friendship and loyalty, she gives them for good, and she forms an enduring bond with Jennifer and Julie, schoolfriends from very different backgrounds. As they grow into the world of the seventies and eighties , the lives of the three best friends are changed forever by two young men, Robin and Jack, and a tragedy which engulfs them all. Against the odds, Tully emerges int</span>
  <span id="freeText5723870225379258873" style="display:none">Tully Makker is a tough young woman from the wrong side of the tracks and she is not always easy to like. But if Tully gives friendship and loyalty, she gives them for good, and she forms an enduring bond with Jennifer and Julie, schoolfriends from very different backgrounds. As they grow into the world of the seventies and eighties , the lives of the three best friends are changed forever by two young men, Robin and Jack, and a tragedy which engulfs them all. Against the odds, Tully emerges into young womanhood, marriage and a career. At last Tully Makker has life under control. And then life strikes back into the most unexpected way of all...<br /><br />This is a very 'real' novel. I felt I could identify with Tully in so many ways. The question is did she make the right choice?</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8325705789802608030">I’m thankful I read this book slowly. Snails pace really. Because it was hard. So hard. Not in a negative way. But in a “it made my heart hurt” way. My feelings hurt. My eyes hurt. My head even started to hurt. Tully is a lost soul. Her whole life. I can’t relate to that personally, but Paullina made me feel for her. You’d think she a weak person, bending easily with the pushes and pulls. But she’s not. She’s strong, fierce. She’s just lost. Lost to her thought. And her voice. I’ll be thinking a</span>
  <span id="freeText8325705789802608030" style="display:none">I’m thankful I read this book slowly. Snails pace really. Because it was hard. So hard. Not in a negative way. But in a “it made my heart hurt” way. My feelings hurt. My eyes hurt. My head even started to hurt. Tully is a lost soul. Her whole life. I can’t relate to that personally, but Paullina made me feel for her. You’d think she a weak person, bending easily with the pushes and pulls. But she’s not. She’s strong, fierce. She’s just lost. Lost to her thought. And her voice. I’ll be thinking about Tully for a long while. And I think she’d be happy knowing she’s thought about.</span>

<div id="review_729554731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729554731" />
    <a title="Justine Crandles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9278437-justine-crandles"><img alt="Justine Crandles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546985799p2/9278437.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/729554731?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine Crandles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine Crandles" href="/user/show/9278437-justine-crandles">Justine Crandles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729554731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8317586628383816753">In 2012 I was introduced to Paulina Simmons and The Bronze Horseman series. I fell in love… with Tatiana and Alexander, their story of love and courage during WWII, and the writing of Simmons. A brilliant story teller and detailed character developer, Simmons drew me in from page one. Jess, one of my beautiful friends and book clubber insisted we all read Tully, Simmons literary debut. A lengthy 600 pager, it was a while before I felt ready to give this novel a go. I am certainly glad I did.<br/><br/>Tull</span>
  <span id="freeText8317586628383816753" style="display:none">In 2012 I was introduced to Paulina Simmons and The Bronze Horseman series. I fell in love… with Tatiana and Alexander, their story of love and courage during WWII, and the writing of Simmons. A brilliant story teller and detailed character developer, Simmons drew me in from page one. Jess, one of my beautiful friends and book clubber insisted we all read Tully, Simmons literary debut. A lengthy 600 pager, it was a while before I felt ready to give this novel a go. I am certainly glad I did.<br /><br />Tully begins with the high school days of our titled character and her two best friends Jennifer and Julie. Set in windswept Kansas, America in the 1970’s, we witness what an abusive childhood has done for Tully now that she is a young adult, and how she copes with love, lies, grief and disaster. The novel is about passion and loss, growing up and moving on, and ultimately decision making; do you follow your heart or head?<br /><br />Tully’s emergence into womanhood demonstrates the importance, or burden, of family, and how we all need to feel loved and important. Her coming of age story, although beautifully written in fascinating detail and emotion, is continually frustrating. Tully never really finds a way to make peace with her past or deal with her issues. This is interesting considering the career she works incredibly hard to make important headway with; child care and fostering and neglected and abused children. This frustrates me to no end. How does she expect to have a happy and healthy relationship and future is she can’t make peace with her demons? What is even more frustrating is her inability to make the right decision. Over and over we see her decide on a new path in life that is not based on what her heart truly desires. Her decisions are clearly based on keeping other people happy or her unwillingness to emulate any of the mistakes her mother or father made when raising her (even though she is clearly an acutely different person than either of her parents).<br /><br />As frustrated as I was with the female protagonist, I was happy to be in a certain way. This type of connection and involvement with a character is what a great author is able to achieve. Simmons’ ability to create characters that you can empathise with, and even more so, feel angry at, is an achievement. If you aren’t that invested in a story or the characters you wouldn’t really care what they did and how it all ended. I was so involved in this story that I felt like I was Tully’s neighbourhood friend who had their own opinions about how she lived her constantly up-heaving life and just wanted to sit her down and give her some good woman to woman advice!<br /><br />The conclusion of the text again had me concerned about how and why Tully decided on incredibly important aspects of her life. However I felt her life was more at peace than it was on page one, and for that I felt a sense of relief. This is a heart wrenching text which I highly recommend. The story of Robin, Shaky, Jack and Tully’s high school and what turns out to be, life long friends, is a beautiful piece of prose. The lead character is full of complexity, is dynamic and passionate, and above all, incredibly interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8317586628383816753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_983956716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/983956716" />
    <a title="Andie Murray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5036591-andie-murray"><img alt="Andie Murray" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316113385p2/5036591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/983956716?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andie Murray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andie Murray" href="/user/show/5036591-andie-murray">Andie Murray</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5036591-andie-murray?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer983956716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6389452039137036943">This book reminded me of She's Come Undone, by Wally Lamb, a little bit. I liked the character development of Tully, but many of the other characters seemed to be relevant only in how they revolved around Tully. The pace of the book is relatively slow, which didn't bother me, but be aware it is a character/relationship study and is not concerned with any particular suspense or action. <br/><br/>As some of the other reviewers have said, Tully isn't really a very likable or relatable person. The author atte</span>
  <span id="freeText6389452039137036943" style="display:none">This book reminded me of She's Come Undone, by Wally Lamb, a little bit. I liked the character development of Tully, but many of the other characters seemed to be relevant only in how they revolved around Tully. The pace of the book is relatively slow, which didn't bother me, but be aware it is a character/relationship study and is not concerned with any particular suspense or action. <br /><br />As some of the other reviewers have said, Tully isn't really a very likable or relatable person. The author attempts to make her more real thru the use of her childhood traumas, abusive mother, and absent father, but I still found it difficult to like Tully, as she kind of went thru life making poor choice after poor choice after yet more poor choices. <br /><br />Yet, I'd still say I liked the book. It stirred up emotions in me and I found myself rooting for Robin, or Jack, by turns. I recommend this book to those who liked She's Come Undone, or other raw, depressing stories about women. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6389452039137036943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1481926670399027264">I hated this book when I read it. I skimmed a lot of it. But I was on a long, long road trip and ended up reading it again. Tully is not always a likable character. And there is some distance between her and the reader, which I'm going to guess Simons did on purpose. You kind of have to figure out why Tully is doing some of the awful things she does.But there are reasons--huge reasons--and after another read through, Tully made sense to me. My heart went out to her. She pushes people away and it</span>
  <span id="freeText1481926670399027264" style="display:none">I hated this book when I read it. I skimmed a lot of it. But I was on a long, long road trip and ended up reading it again. Tully is not always a likable character. And there is some distance between her and the reader, which I'm going to guess Simons did on purpose. You kind of have to figure out why Tully is doing some of the awful things she does.But there are reasons--huge reasons--and after another read through, Tully made sense to me. My heart went out to her. She pushes people away and it takes her a long, long time to get over her past. <br /><br />So in the end this was a thought provoking read. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pEpNWjeEgyVI6i/hK6biquDAEBvqlrDINXLyk8QTZshMZW1a5F1iiLWOpt+s9VH6Lvb8Kn7XPepQUp1sCaiYvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/47499.Paullina_Simons">About Paullina Simons</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/47499.Paullina_Simons"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1263597025p3/47499.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8111136628934812148">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br/><br/>After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullin</span>
  <span id="freeText8111136628934812148" style="display:none">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br /><br />After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullina wrote her first novel <i>Tully</i>. Through word of mouth that book was welcomed by readers all over the world. <br /><br />She continued with more novels, including <i>Red Leaves, Eleven Hours, The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i> (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>), <i>The Summer Garden</i> and <i>The Girl in Times Square</i> (also known as <i>Lily</i>). Many of Paullina's novels have reached international bestseller lists. <br /><br />Apart from her novels, Paullina has also written a cookbook, <i>Tatiana's Table</i>, which is a collection of recipes, short stories and recollections from her best selling trilogy of novels, <i>The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i>, (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>) and <i>The Summer Garden</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8111136628934812148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
